  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9b8f6ed2-e488-467f-a114-59bf3f51a0b8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText6425897135100069873" style="display:none">Sonea, once the despised commoner in the Magicians' Guild, is now a Black Magician of Kyralia. Though she is now part of the establishment, she comes to find that the past is not so easily left behind... <br />Lorkin, Sonea's rebellious son, has volunteered to join the formidable Lord Dannyl in his new post as Guild Ambassador to Sachaka - a land ruled by cruel, slave-owning black magicians. There is suspicion that some of the Sachakans still harbor dreams of conquest, so when word comes that Lorkin has gone missing, Sonea is desperate to find him. However, Guild law states that if a Black Magician leaves the city he or she will be exiled forever. <br />As she fears for her missing son, Sonea dedicates herself to helping her old friend Cery. For some time, there has been fear and paranoia on the streets of Imardin. Leading thieves have been dying under irregular circumstances. The need to discover who has been picking off the leading thieves of the city is now a very personal crusade - one that Sonea must aid, for the killer appears to be using magic. <br />Either a member of the Guild is leading a double life as a hired killer, or there is - once again - a rogue magician on the streets of Imardin . . .</span>

<a href="/questions/930314-can-this-be-read-without-having-read-the">Can this be read without having read the Black Magician series? I do plan on reading that series soonish, but I would like to read the traitor&#39;s spy trilogy first, if possible</a>
</div>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/52099135-audrey-leigh-hughes"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1490030538i/52099135._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
Read the Black Magician series first. The events that happen in The Traitor Spy Trilogy occur after the Black Magician series.
</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_331571612" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/331571612" />
    <a title="Allison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9371994-allison"><img alt="Allison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461856985p2/9371994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/331571612?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/9371994-allison">Allison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8439097-the-ambassador-s-mission">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=own-ebook">own-ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=series-complete">series-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=spinoff">spinoff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=witches-wizards-mages">witches-wizards-mages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=series-i-finished">series-i-finished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=published-2010s">published-2010s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=thieves">thieves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331571612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer862811296356902331">I was really disappointed in this. I've loved Canavan's previous work - she's one of my favorite authors! But something went wrong here. It was just so incredibly boring. There's not enough that's new, but instead a lot of time is spent explaining how things have changed from 20 years ago, or rediscovering the past that has already been explored in the <i>Magician's Apprentice.</i> I think Canavan would have been better off building a whole new world with new conflicts and magic rather than re-hashing </span>
  <span id="freeText862811296356902331" style="display:none">I was really disappointed in this. I've loved Canavan's previous work - she's one of my favorite authors! But something went wrong here. It was just so incredibly boring. There's not enough that's new, but instead a lot of time is spent explaining how things have changed from 20 years ago, or rediscovering the past that has already been explored in the <i>Magician's Apprentice.</i> I think Canavan would have been better off building a whole new world with new conflicts and magic rather than re-hashing a world and characters that I already know and love. <br /><br />What <i>is</i> new is the character of Lorkin, but I really can't tell you much about him. I don't feel that he is well-defined enough, although I hope that improves in the next books. There is so much reminiscing about the past by return characters that we don't get a clear enough sense of the present and why we should care about it. <br /><br />I mainly just felt nostalgic for the days of the Ichani invasion, and felt like I was having sumi with my old friends from the war, chatting about how times have changed and feeling sad that they haven't turned out better after all that effort. I can't believe I'm writing this - I had such hopes for this sequel!<br /><br />There are really two distinct plots in the book. One is Lorkin's adventures in Sachaka. Apparently he wants to find old magic for some reason, but I don't really feel his excitement or know why it's important enough to him to risk his life going there. He just seems to want a grown-up adventure and a chance to prove himself. The unasked-for adventures that he gets should be a lot more exciting, but the gripping, engaging aspect of the previous books is missing. <br /><br />The other plot sticks with Cery and Sonea in their separate spheres in Imardin. It's sort of a murder mystery, but it's hard to care because you're mainly getting the characters' inner dialogue on what's changed in the last 20 years, or speculating about how a situation could go 3 different ways. And there's not nearly enough magic to help make up for it - what there is is just incidental, like opening and closing doors, and some levitation. I think I've made my point by now - it just really dragged.<br /><br />Can I also say that Sonea being an overprotective mother is not what I want to read about? That's the main addition to her character in this, other than the fact that she's been stuck in the same restrictions for the last 20 years. She really needs to move on from the past and find a way to gain the trust of the Guild so she can do more than work in the hospices. I expect (hope) that what happens in the rest of the trilogy gives her a way to do that, and to let her son be an adult. In other words, I'll have to go ahead and read the rest of the trilogy and hope it gets better. It's too late to turn back now.<br /><br />Honestly, what's missing is the one person who can't make an encore appearance. No wonder it's so lackluster - all of the true mystery and the reason for everyone's existence is gone. The best character EVER leaves a gaping hole. <br /><br />I am now more upset than ever that <i>The High Lord</i> ended the way it did. It could have had a way happier ending, everything resolved to some degree and - finished. Complete. I could have been so happy. Why? Why?<br /><br />I WANT MY OLD BLACK MAGICIAN BACK!!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="862811296356902331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9674045319577151073" style="display:none">I hate writing poor reviews, but I was very disappointed by this book. The BMT shares joint first place in my top fantasy series, and I was so looking forward to this. <br /><br />The characters are all flat and insipid - even those who were previously exciting and well fleshed-out; the constant references to the previous trilogy were irritating (I read that trilogy several times already and I read it again before I read this book, I don't need to be told every single thing that happened in it!); the quality of the language itself was poor as well, like it was written for a very young child. <br /><br />All of the faults I found caused me to give up about two thirds of the way through, something I rarely do. <div id="review_173123195" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173123195" />
    <a title="Crazyjamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3025308-crazyjamie"><img alt="Crazyjamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321964208p2/3025308.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/173123195?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crazyjamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crazyjamie" href="/user/show/3025308-crazyjamie">Crazyjamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer173123195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6980483066809453128">In reading terms, I think I owe Trudi Canavan quite a lot. I say that because the Black Magician trilogy was the first set of books that I read away from the truly mainstream series such as Harry Potter. From the Black Magician trilogy I went on to Age of Five, and from there my reading really took off. So I very much see Trudi Canavan as the first author that wasn't in some way pushed on to me by public perception (not that I resent Harry Potter for that, but the distinction is important). What</span>
  <span id="freeText6980483066809453128" style="display:none">In reading terms, I think I owe Trudi Canavan quite a lot. I say that because the Black Magician trilogy was the first set of books that I read away from the truly mainstream series such as Harry Potter. From the Black Magician trilogy I went on to Age of Five, and from there my reading really took off. So I very much see Trudi Canavan as the first author that wasn't in some way pushed on to me by public perception (not that I resent Harry Potter for that, but the distinction is important). What's more, the Black Magician trilogy remains one of my favourite fantasy series, and as such it was with significant anticipation that I started to read the Ambassador's Mission, the first in the sequel trilogy to the Black Magician trilogy. <br /><br />The Ambassador's Mission is set 20 years after the end of the Black Magician Trilogy. Sonea is a Black Magician within the Magician's Guild, but with black magic still illegal in the country, there is a further magician within the Guild who has been trained to the same level. Thankfully a lot of familiar faces return, with the likes of Dannyl, Rothen, Regin and Cery all playing significant parts in the new story. Of the new characters, the most notable is Lorkin, Sonea's son. The plot of the first book sees Dannyl and Sonea traveling to Sachaka in search of answers to questions surrounding the history of the Guild and Imardin in general. Back in the city itself, thieves are being murdered by a rogue magician, and Cery attempts to track the rogue down with the help of Skellin, the most powerful thief in the city. <br /><br />The trademark characteristic of Canavan's writing is that she manages to write adult novels that are incredibly accessible to all ages, and the books set in this world have also had the added bonus of being suitable for a wide range of ages as well. I am happy to say that the Ambassador's Mission continues this trend, with interesting characters and easy flowing dialogue. It's the sort of book that you can become absorbed in and feel like you are involved in rather than simply observing from a distance. <br /><br />The real joy of this book is seeing how the familiar characters have evolved in two decades, and in this regard the book certainly doesn't disappoint, but the new characters are worthy additions to the cast as well, and give the plot a sense of freshness. There is no element of repetition in terms of plot here; despite familiar characters, the book constantly feels like it is treading new ground and building on the story from the previous series. <br /><br />The only criticism that can be aimed at this first book is that it is not quite as dynamic as other standout fantasy books. The magic system is simple and doesn't provide standout entertainment by itself, and whilst there are some good action sequences, set pieces and twists, the book feels a little lightweight overall. This is especially so when compared to the likes of the Black Prism, which is another first book in a trilogy that I read recently. However, it remains an accessible and enjoyable read in the classic Canavan style. It also sets things up in an intriguing fashion for the next book, so if you are a Canavan fan, this is essential reading. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6980483066809453128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ithlilian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ithlilian" href="/user/show/4793655-ithlilian">Ithlilian</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4793655-ithlilian?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140318747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1959366341254827868">The Ambassador's Mission is much better than The Magician's Apprentice, but no where near as entertaining as The Black Magician Trilogy. The plot can be summed up as follows: someone is killing thieves, and Lorkin goes for a long walk in Sachaka. The characters are no where near as dynamic and interesting as they were in The Black Magician Trilogy. Cery is old and worn out, Sonea is tepid and uninteresting. Lorkin isn't any more exciting than anyone else. If this book was written by anyone else </span>
  <span id="freeText1959366341254827868" style="display:none">The Ambassador's Mission is much better than The Magician's Apprentice, but no where near as entertaining as The Black Magician Trilogy. The plot can be summed up as follows: someone is killing thieves, and Lorkin goes for a long walk in Sachaka. The characters are no where near as dynamic and interesting as they were in The Black Magician Trilogy. Cery is old and worn out, Sonea is tepid and uninteresting. Lorkin isn't any more exciting than anyone else. If this book was written by anyone else I don't think I would have finished it, but Trudi Canavan has something that I like. It may be the large amount of dialogue, the magic, or the guild environment that kept me interested in this novel, but I'm not sure if I will be continuing. There isn't much reason to really. There are power gems that may be important, and some foreigners that are dangerous, but it's just not enough. There is no sense of urgency or danger, everything is just blah. If you are a fan of The Black Magician Trilogy give this a try to brush up on your favorite characters and revisit the world, but don't expect it to be as exciting as the original trilogy. </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer299987096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9474673326081383752">A decade ago, when I read “The Magician’s Guild”, the first of the “Black Magician Trilogy”, I was filled with excitement. Young Sonea’s struggle with her new found powers, her attempts to understand and survive the upper-class world she was pushed into and the complex loyalties she had to navigate had immediate appeal and, although it was a long book, kept me eagerly turning the pages to find out what happened next.<br/><br/>For me, “The Ambassador’s Mission”, the first volume in the “Traitor Spy” trilog</span>
  <span id="freeText9474673326081383752" style="display:none">A decade ago, when I read “The Magician’s Guild”, the first of the “Black Magician Trilogy”, I was filled with excitement. Young Sonea’s struggle with her new found powers, her attempts to understand and survive the upper-class world she was pushed into and the complex loyalties she had to navigate had immediate appeal and, although it was a long book, kept me eagerly turning the pages to find out what happened next.<br /><br />For me, “The Ambassador’s Mission”, the first volume in the “Traitor Spy” trilogy, has none of the magic I found in the “Magician’s Guild”.<br /><br />It is well written. The ideas are thought through. The characters are as well drawn as in the previous books. Yet the book seems slow. It feels as if Trudi Canavan is thinking: “I have three thick volumes to tell this story, there’s no need to hurry.” Unfortunately, I was left thinking that, if they all go at this pace, I might never make it to the end of book two.<br /><br />Perhaps it is that the Sonea is now older and more reflective, she has become part of the establishment, while Cery has become an old thief and the head of a family. Perhaps it is just the need to connect this book to the “Black Magician Trilogy” and its prequel, “The Magician’s Apprentice” but I found that I did not have the same passion for these characters and the challenges that they face.<br /><br />In “The Magician’s Apprentice”, it mattered to me whether it would be Lord Rothen or the treacherous Lord Fergun who had power over Sonea. In “The Ambassador’s Mission” the death of the whole family of one of the characters barely created an emotional ripple.<br /><br />As a generation-spanning, fantasy-saga, dealing with a complex world, this is still a book worth reading but set against the last trilogy, I found it disappointing.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9474673326081383752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_614413768" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/614413768" />
    <a title="Maurine Tritch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1220877-maurine-tritch"><img alt="Maurine Tritch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601591074p2/1220877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/614413768?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maurine Tritch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maurine Tritch" href="/user/show/1220877-maurine-tritch">Maurine Tritch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer614413768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5685951695843141161">I enjoyed reading the continuing story of Sonea and company, but this book had major problems. The first and foremost being that it started in the wrong place. The Ambassador's Mission dealt with two plotlines: the tale of the new Ambassador (Dannyl) and his assistant--Sonea's and Akkarin's son, Lorkin--to the neighboring country that caused all the problems in the first trilogy. The second plot is the insidious corruption at home, of an irresistable drug that turns people to mindless addicts in</span>
  <span id="freeText5685951695843141161" style="display:none">I enjoyed reading the continuing story of Sonea and company, but this book had major problems. The first and foremost being that it started in the wrong place. The Ambassador's Mission dealt with two plotlines: the tale of the new Ambassador (Dannyl) and his assistant--Sonea's and Akkarin's son, Lorkin--to the neighboring country that caused all the problems in the first trilogy. The second plot is the insidious corruption at home, of an irresistable drug that turns people to mindless addicts in a single dose, and a rogue magician hunting Thieves. The book should have opened with Lorkin arriving in Sachaka. Then tedious arguements over whether or not he should go, the persuading of his mother, and viewing of his friends' dangerous habits could be dealt with in a couple of memories. Ditto with Dannyl's flagging relationship with his beloved. Cery's story should have started when he asked Sonea for help, again avoiding chapters of useless buildup that wasn't aided by our witnessing it since Cery didn't either. Basically, half the book was wasted in minutia. Once it got going, Cery's story was very a leads to b, without many surprises or real suspense; Lorkin's story was much more interesting but unfortunately he is not. He has none of his mother's fortitude or his father's passion and mystery, he's just sort of there: immature and obnoxious, a typical guy. This could change, I suppose. So all in all, I was disappointed but am still planning to read further.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5685951695843141161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_353836366" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/353836366" />
    <a title="Mjhancock" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3897241-mjhancock"><img alt="Mjhancock" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/353836366?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mjhancock" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mjhancock" href="/user/show/3897241-mjhancock">Mjhancock</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3897241-mjhancock?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer353836366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6735914277818948932">Ambassador's Mission is the first book in Trudi Canavan's Traitor Spy Trilogy, and it takes place about two decades after her previous trilogy, the Black Magician. A lot of the characters are carried over between the two series, but if you haven't read the first one (or you're just very forgetful, like me), it's fairly easy to establish who's who. The plot quickly splits in two, with Sonea becoming embroiled in uncovering a plot to kill the city's head thieves while her son gets into diplomatic </span>
  <span id="freeText6735914277818948932" style="display:none">Ambassador's Mission is the first book in Trudi Canavan's Traitor Spy Trilogy, and it takes place about two decades after her previous trilogy, the Black Magician. A lot of the characters are carried over between the two series, but if you haven't read the first one (or you're just very forgetful, like me), it's fairly easy to establish who's who. The plot quickly splits in two, with Sonea becoming embroiled in uncovering a plot to kill the city's head thieves while her son gets into diplomatic intrigue in a neighboring country. There's a lot to like here. Canavan pulls off the dual plots rather well, and manages to transition her protagonist from the single young woman in the first series to a middle-aged (or close to) mother in this series without losing the core of what made Sonea an appealing character to begin with. On the downside, one of the plots takes a turn where the reader is all but screaming at the protagonists to stop being idiots. And, more importantly, it's hard to shake the feeling that very little has happened by the book's end. Rather than resolve any of the major issues, it's more like everyone's been moved into their places for the next book. It's understandable, given this is the first book in a trilogy, but a little disappointing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6735914277818948932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_585628756" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/585628756" />
    <a title="Ian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19074825-ian"><img alt="Ian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594416438p2/19074825.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/585628756?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian" href="/user/show/19074825-ian">Ian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841495927" href="/book/show/7815982-the-ambassador-s-mission">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19074825-ian?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer585628756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8485123969534005646">You can also read this review at <a href='http://anotherworldbookblog.wordpress.com/2014/09/15/review-the-ambassadors-mission-by-trudi-canavan/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Another World</a>, (The Fantasy & Science Fiction Book Blog).<br/><br/><br/> There is an adage which teaches us that, “you should never go back”. This saying is usually used in reference to romantic relationships, but perhaps it should also serve as a warning to authors wanting to revisit past glories. Though the temptation to do so is, of course, perfectly understandable. Returning to the scene of a previous triumph no doubt seems like the safe and easy path to take; but how often</span>
  <span id="freeText8485123969534005646" style="display:none">You can also read this review at <a href="http://anotherworldbookblog.wordpress.com/2014/09/15/review-the-ambassadors-mission-by-trudi-canavan/" rel="nofollow noopener">Another World</a>, (The Fantasy &amp; Science Fiction Book Blog).<br><br><br> There is an adage which teaches us that, “you should never go back”. This saying is usually used in reference to romantic relationships, but perhaps it should also serve as a warning to authors wanting to revisit past glories. Though the temptation to do so is, of course, perfectly understandable. Returning to the scene of a previous triumph no doubt seems like the safe and easy path to take; but how often does it turn out not to be the case? Certainly, The Ambassador’s Mission, provides a perfect illustration as to the wisdom of the words, “you should never go back”.<br><br> I cannot fault author, Trudi Canavan, for believing a sequel trilogy to her most successful work would be a win-win proposition. The Black Magician Trilogy was well received by critics, and loved by many readers; earning her a legion of fans. A return to the Allied Lands, twenty years after the events of the previous trilogy, to revisit an adult Sonea in a new adventure, sounds like an exciting prospect. Though I had certain misgivings (which I’ll address later) about the book before I began reading, nothing could prepare me for the disappointment that awaited in this first instalment of The Traitor Spy Trilogy. I am not someone who is prone to indulging in hyperbole, but The Ambassador’s Mission is a failure in every conceivable way.<br><br> So what went so drastically wrong? Well let’s start with the most glaringly notable problem first. At no point during the book is the narrative in any way engaging; a criticism I never thought I would ever level at Canavan’s writing. Though actual boredom didn’t quite settle in, the story is so ponderous that extra effort was required to keep turning the pages; all in the vain hope that something of significance would happen. (But it didn’t.)<br><br> Perhaps some of the lack of engagement can be attributed to the plot; or should I say the plots? As there are two distinct, and apparently unconnected, plots running throughout; each one with its own sub-plots. This goes some way to explaining the lack of focus in the narrative, as Canavan tries to give both storylines equal time, hence the constant jumping back and forth between them. But the book would have been better served if the plot involving Sonea’s son Lorkin, was relegated to minor sub-plot status, if not completely excised from the story completely. Focussing on Sonea’s story; assisting Cery track down the rogue magician responsible for the assassinations of several leading figures among the criminal underground known as The Thieves, would have made for a more compelling read.<br><br> Much of my dissatisfaction with the narrative could have been mitigated to some extent, if I felt invested in any of the main characters, which brings me to the most disappointing aspect of the book; poor characterisation. This was very surprising because Canavan is usually so adept at creating such distinct and memorable characters for her stories. On this occasion, however, the exact opposite is the case. The newly introduced characters, who hadn’t featured in The Black Magician Trilogy, are so nondescript that (with the exception of Lorkin) I was never able to remember their names, let alone anything else of consequence about them.<br><br> Even the returning characters, whom I was already familiar with, were shadows of their former selves. In particular, I was less than impressed with the depiction of Sonea. You would assume that a character would have undergone a significant amount of development over a period of two decades, yet Sonea seems very much like the teenage girl that she was in the previous trilogy, not the forty year old mother of an adult son that she is supposed to be in this book.<br><br> I suspect that a lot of the problems present within this book are the result of the author’s decision to write a trilogy at all cost, even if the story she had in mind doesn’t warrant three books. It certainly seems as though the main culprit for the lack of any truly significant moments during the story, was the desire to save everything of interest for the third book. Which explains why The Ambassador’s Mission feels very much like an overly long prologue. And never in my life have I ever encountered such an abrupt ending to a book. Upon reaching the end of the final chapter, only to turn the page and be greeted by an epilogue, I was utterly convinced that my copy of the book must be missing at least a hundred pages. It actually took several minutes to accept that this was not the case.<br><br> It’s hard to believe that all these issues I had with the book, are in no way related to the one thing I had misgivings about before I began reading. With half the story taking place in the land of Sachaka, I was concerned that learning too much about its people and culture would have the effect of de-mystifying the Sachakans. After all, one of the main reasons why they seemed to represent such a threat in The Black Magician Trilogy was that so little was revealed about them; they were a mystery. While The Ambassador’s Mission does indeed de-mystify the Sachakan people, it proves not to be as detrimental as I had feared, given how flawed the rest of the book is.<br><br> In summation, book one of The Traitor Spy Trilogy is a very disappointing affair. For readers who are not pre-existing fans of Trudi Canavan, there is little here to warrant reading the rest of the trilogy. But she has earned enough good will from me that I shall finish reading the next two instalments. Although I am now beginning to wonder if Canavan will prove to be a one trick pony, if not an actual one hit wonder.<br><br><br><br><a href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/3.0/deed.en_GB" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="Creative Commons Licence" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379791738i/554143.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8485123969534005646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<span id="freeTextContainer11144421553890947186">Enjoyable but a bit slow to start with the pace picKing up further in. This trilogy is set 20 years after the last and, obviously, there was a lot to fill in, hence the laborious feel. But now the story is really set in motion I think the trilogy will only get stronger and I'm looking forward to carrying on with book 2. Only slight irritation- I was surprised by Sonea's somewhat wishy-washy character until nearly the end; I remember her as a lot stronger and more pro-active in the 1st trilogy.</span>

<div id="review_136023749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136023749" />
    <a title="Ranting Dragon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4367400-ranting-dragon"><img alt="Ranting Dragon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1317746155p2/4367400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136023749?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ranting Dragon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ranting Dragon" href="/user/show/4367400-ranting-dragon">Ranting Dragon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4367400-ranting-dragon?shelf=caitrin">caitrin</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136023749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16386665361336822553"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.rantingdragon.com/the-ambassadors-mission-by-trudi-canavan/'>http://www.rantingdragon.com/the-amba...</a><br/><br/><br/>Trudi Canavan is an Australian author best known for her Black Magician trilogy starring Sonea, a slum child hunted for using magic reserved for the higher classes. The Traitor Spy Trilogy is set 20 years later with Sonea as one of two Black Magicians in the Magicians Guild and is limited to Guild grounds and the Hospices that offer free healing throughout the city. When the Magicians Guild is opens to all magic-users, tensions arise because of old prejudi</span>
  <span id="freeText16386665361336822553" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.rantingdragon.com/the-ambassadors-mission-by-trudi-canavan/">http://www.rantingdragon.com/the-amba...</a><br /><br /><br />Trudi Canavan is an Australian author best known for her Black Magician trilogy starring Sonea, a slum child hunted for using magic reserved for the higher classes. The Traitor Spy Trilogy is set 20 years later with Sonea as one of two Black Magicians in the Magicians Guild and is limited to Guild grounds and the Hospices that offer free healing throughout the city. When the Magicians Guild is opens to all magic-users, tensions arise because of old prejudices between the classes. Meanwhile a drug that is so addictive that it can’t seem to be healed away even from Magicians whose bodies normally fight any kind of disease.<br /><br />Without reading previous novels Canavan drops enough of the history that you won’t feel lost or confused at any point in the novel.<br /><br />Assassins in the Night<br />Lorkin, Sonea’s son, has graduated and is unsure of what he wants to do with his talents. An opportunity comes up to travel as an assistant with Ambassador Dannyl to Sachaka, a land where those who are Magicians are only Black Magicians and the culture is strongly tied to slavery unlike his homeland. Lorkin wants to research the history of magic in order to find something that will help Kyralia, during which he wakes up to an assassination attempt and flees with the slave that saves him.<br /><br />Murder Most Foul<br />Cery is a Thief from the previous novels who now has a wife, two sons and an estranged daughter. He attends a meeting with the new head of the Thieves Guild, a man he doesn’t know much about except that his name is Skellin, who asks him to find the notorious Thief Hunter who has been killing off Thieves. When he returns home he discovers his family has been murdered and he suspects it’s the Thief Hunter who may be a magician. He enlists the help of a former friend, Sonea, and together they try to find the Thief Hunter.<br /><br />Flat-lining<br />While I feel like the novel was solid, it felt a bit average. It was neither bad nor was it really good. The worldbuilding was strong and I’d like to see more of the world. I found the hunt for the Thief Hunter to be engaging and the mystery of it was the best part of the novel. Cery and his companions were the most interesting and fleshed out, on the other hand, Lorkin’s escape lacked suspense and his romance with his fellow escapee lacked substance. He seemed to fall in love with the woman for no real reason and she with him. It may have felt differently if I’d read the previous trilogy but I felt Sonea’s characterization was weak as if the author relied on the previous novels to supply most of her characterization. She always seemed to be reacting to the circumstances she was in rather than taking charge. Overall The Ambassador’s Mission was a fun, light read that felt like a set-up for later events in the story.<br /><br />Sequal-ity<br />The book has a strong ending that brings some closure in the Thief Hunter being discovered, but also creates questions that make me interested in the sequel. The “end” of Lorkin’s storyline also had a strong resolution, but his future, both with the romantic interest and with The Traitors is unclear. It definitely creates more interest in the sequel and is one of the best parts of the book. I think the next book is going to be even better because it doesn’t suffer from being the first novel in the series with all of the set-up.<br /><br />Why you should read this book?<br />If you’re looking for a traditional light fantasy I think you’ll enjoy The Ambassador’s Mission. Beginner fantasy readers or readers who’ve read The Black Magician trilogy will also enjoy the book. If you’re looking for something different or deep though, I think you’ll be a bit bored.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16386665361336822553" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16530110-emmeline-the-book-herald?shelf=romance">romance</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16530110-emmeline-the-book-herald?shelf=epic">epic</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1243450515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer607186254173986395"><b>That world Building!</b> <br/><br/>This book was huge, like nearly 600 pages...and for 600 pages it was non-stop action!<br/><br/>I loved this world building, I loved the idea of it too. <br/><br/>what I wasn't a ginormous fan of is the large amount of POVs. <br/>That may be more of a personal issue but usually when there are more than a three person POV, I just get tired, but I'll go more into that in a moment. <br/><br/><u>LET'S TALK PLOT!</u><br/><br/><i>In this land is where magicians rule in guilds but those who are practitioners of 'black' magic are feared </i></span>
  <span id="freeText607186254173986395" style="display:none"><b>That world Building!</b> <br /><br />This book was huge, like nearly 600 pages...and for 600 pages it was non-stop action!<br /><br />I loved this world building, I loved the idea of it too. <br /><br />what I wasn't a ginormous fan of is the large amount of POVs. <br />That may be more of a personal issue but usually when there are more than a three person POV, I just get tired, but I'll go more into that in a moment. <br /><br /><u>LET'S TALK PLOT!</u><br /><br /><i>In this land is where magicians rule in guilds but those who are practitioners of 'black' magic are feared and nearly chained to their rooms.<br />Where Thieves rule and kill one another.<br />Where a boy seeks to live up to his father's hero status. <br />There is plotting in the darkness of that land. <br /><br />Cery is a thief who rules the North, his family was assassinated, and suddenly no one is able to live without looking over their shoulders.<br />A thief-hunter wants to destroy them all and has killed many. <br />who is it or what is it? <br />Cery seeks the aid of Black magician Sonea and the two find themselves in a lot more trouble than they originally anticipated. <br /><br />Sonea's son wants to live up to his father's heroic status as the one who saved the land. <br />He promptly decides to become the Ambassador's assistant to a turbulent land but finds himself a murder target instead. <br />He is rescued by a girl. <br />He discovers a wild magic unlike any he has ever seen. <br />what more will he discover? </i><br /><br />okay so as a Fantasy this one was pretty good. However, I didn't really connect with any of the characters. <br />It's extremely inventive and really ingenious, but the way it started made me feel like i was reading the second or third book rather than the first. I had to constantly remind myself what was what, therefore, the back of the book with the index page became my best friend. <br /><br />The romance wasn't swoon- worthy to me. It's actually pretty minimal. <br />Not in the ways i usually liked but maybe that's because i didn't really <i>feel</i> invested in these characters. <br /><br />Overall pretty good. The writing was good but I didn't have that Alice feeling of just falling into that world. <br /><br />Have a go at it, you may enjoy it loads more than i did! :)<br /><br />Stay awesome!<br /><br />-The Book Herald </span>

<div id="review_141699452" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/141699452" />
    <a title="Nickey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4829816-nickey"><img alt="Nickey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296681983p2/4829816.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/141699452?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nickey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nickey" href="/user/show/4829816-nickey">Nickey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Trudi Canavan</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer141699452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6034352074424589818">I was surprised to find myself struggling though this book. I have read seven other of Trudi Canavan's books and got through most of them within two or three days. This time it took me over a week.<br/><br/>I think the two main problems are that I read The Magician's Apprentice before this one and that Canavan placed this story twenty years after the Black Magician Trilogy.<br/><br/>Due to the circumstance that I knew a lot of the historical aspects of the story world from TMA it was very unnerving and almost borin</span>
  <span id="freeText6034352074424589818" style="display:none">I was surprised to find myself struggling though this book. I have read seven other of Trudi Canavan's books and got through most of them within two or three days. This time it took me over a week.<br /><br />I think the two main problems are that I read The Magician's Apprentice before this one and that Canavan placed this story twenty years after the Black Magician Trilogy.<br /><br />Due to the circumstance that I knew a lot of the historical aspects of the story world from TMA it was very unnerving and almost boring to have Lorkin and Dannyl slowly stumble upon bits and pieces of the same throughout the plot. It wouldn't have hurt the book to loose a good 100 pages in the beginning - that would have quickened the pace and given room to actual, new information.<br /><br />The second, for me much bigger, problem was the time difference between The Black Magician Trilogy and The Ambassador's Mission. Before, most of the main characters were more or less my age - now they are suddenly twenty years older and they didn't exactly develop the way I would have liked them.<br />Sonea has grown timid and scared to do a misstep. I would have loved to see her explode and do what SHE thinks is right. She is still grieving over the loss of Akkarin and yet she lets the Guild decide to let Lorkin go without putting up fight. Where has all her fight gone? <br />Regin has turned nice. NICE? Hello?<br />And Cerry is old. Even he keeps pointing that out. Following a twenty-something around town chasing a murderer is fun and exciting - following a forty-something is just painful. It says a lot that still his plot arch was the one that I enjoyed the most.<br />Dannyl hasn't actually changed that much, it's just that his quest for more research is rather boring to the facts mentioned above.<br />And newcomer Lorkin, I don't see much of either of his parents in him. Canavan had to actually point it out to her readers. All in all he seems shallowly written and I can't follow his decision making process at all. His behaviour just seems irrational.<br /><br />I can only hope that The Rogue is going to be MUCH better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6034352074424589818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1677282523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1677282523" />
    <a title="Tommye Turner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30506556-tommye-turner"><img alt="Tommye Turner" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1677282523?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tommye Turner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tommye Turner" href="/user/show/30506556-tommye-turner">Tommye Turner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30506556-tommye-turner?shelf=fantasy-read">fantasy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1677282523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3076793312356371130">SPOILER FREE<br/><br/>It can happen so often that a writer returns with a sequel book or series to a previously complete story and then completely ruin it. Even bringing back a few familiar faces can’t fix it. <br/><br/>This book didn’t need to fix anything. Even if she didn’t, it feels like Canavan knew where this story was going right from the beginning of the first trilogy. There were a few unanswered questions at the end of The High Lord, which I had first believed to be for the reader to theorise about for the</span>
  <span id="freeText3076793312356371130" style="display:none">SPOILER FREE<br /><br />It can happen so often that a writer returns with a sequel book or series to a previously complete story and then completely ruin it. Even bringing back a few familiar faces can’t fix it. <br /><br />This book didn’t need to fix anything. Even if she didn’t, it feels like Canavan knew where this story was going right from the beginning of the first trilogy. There were a few unanswered questions at the end of The High Lord, which I had first believed to be for the reader to theorise about for the rest of their lives – instead we were treated to a few new answers and even more questions!<br /><br />Canavan does mystery well. We are given small clues, our protagonist moves the story forwards in order to discover the answers only to find out that the questions weren’t quite the right ones, or that there’s an even bigger reveal that we first thought. It makes for an exciting read and one that leaves you unable to put the book down!<br /><br />Sonea’s son, Lorkin is our main protagonist in this trilogy. He’s so much like Sonea when it comes to his passion and drive, but having grown up in privileged, his outlook on life is subtly different to hers. He is faced with the crimes of his father – a man he never knew – and this makes for an intriguing character-driven story arc, alongside the main plot. <br /><br />This is a fantastic addition to the world Canavan realised in The Black Magician trilogy. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3076793312356371130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3373987853" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3373987853" />
    <a title="Veronica Ika " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18173496-veronica-ika"><img alt="Veronica Ika " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566828461p2/18173496.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3373987853?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronica Ika " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronica Ika " href="/user/show/18173496-veronica-ika">Veronica Ika </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18173496-veronica-ika?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18173496-veronica-ika?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18173496-veronica-ika?shelf=three-stars">three-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18173496-veronica-ika?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3373987853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9589222001397248316">Being a fan of Black Magician trilogy who have re-read it many times to the extent to which I’ve lost count, I felt utterly exhilarated to find a month ago that there’s a sequel to it. Even though a particular favourite character of mine from the previous trilogy will clearly not make any appearance here -- even my bestie decides to stop finishing the trilogy after I accidentally (oops) spoiled what happened to the said character --, I’m not disappointed because, once again, even after that unfa</span>
  <span id="freeText9589222001397248316" style="display:none">Being a fan of Black Magician trilogy who have re-read it many times to the extent to which I’ve lost count, I felt utterly exhilarated to find a month ago that there’s a sequel to it. Even though a particular favourite character of mine from the previous trilogy will clearly not make any appearance here -- even my bestie decides to stop finishing the trilogy after I accidentally (oops) spoiled what happened to the said character --, I’m not disappointed because, once again, even after that unfair and terrible fate, this character has proven to yet contribute another important role in this sequel. If you’re a fan of Black Magician trilogy, too, this trilogy is definitely a MUST! If you haven’t read the trilogy, I recommend you to do it immediately because I think there is no way you can enjoy this book without reading the previous trilogy. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE OLD AND THE NEW</u>
</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Change goes on all the time. You lose something and you gain something else.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />It is twenty years after the infamous Ichani Invasion. The city of Imardin and the Guild have changed a lot, both for the better and the worse. The better: now the Guild includes two Black magicians in its hierarchy and accept novices from outside of the Houses to the university. The worse: now crimes and dubious activities in the city of Imardin hit a new level of alarming. More novices and magicians from the Houses are involved in immoral habits, the fact that may or may not be exacerbated by the involvement of the novices and magicians from low society who are, mostly, associated with ‘criminals and characters of low repute’. A new drug called roet has mushroomed, and its devastating effects both on common people and magicians cause a great concern. An individual dubbed as the Thief Hunter roams in the city, leaving Thieves dead unnatural deaths in its wake. <br /><br />Amidst of this all turmoil, Sonea, now a Black magician and a mother, is helplessly bound by the rules of the Guild that restricts all her movements. However, how could she stay obedient when Cery, with a target on his back, requests for her help to capture the Thief Hunter, who believes is a rogue magician? When an unlikely ally gives her unlikely support and aid in this unlikely crusade? When she heard that her only son is abducted by a group assumed to be more dangerous than the Sachakan themselves?<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Of course there are risks – there are risks to everything a magician does.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />That’s what Lorkin, the 20-year-old son of Black Magician Sonea and former High Lord Akkarin, says in his defence when he decides to be an assistant to the new Guild Ambassador to Sachaka, Lord Dannyl, despite his mother’s dismay and warnings that some Sachakans may want to take revenge for what his parents did. But his thirst for magical knowledge cannot sway him to venture into Sachaka, a land ruled by slave-owning black magicians. Until one particular fail attempt of assassination and a Traitor named Tyvara. Can he make a right decision that secures not only his safety but also the interest of the Guild? Can Dannyl find and save Lorkin before he must report to the Guild about Lorkin’s missing and possibly incur Sonea’s wrath?<br /><br />Despite my excitement to read this trilogy, I can’t help but once again point out the blemishes of this book that are annoyingly similar to the first book of the previous trilogy. Not to fret over its style of writing, though. <b>It is beautifully written, but it’s dragging!</b> As I’ve mentioned earlier, I recommend you to read High Lord trilogy before reading this trilogy, so a great deal of revisiting to the events in The High Lord is actually a bit unnecessary for me. Some events even seem out of place as if Trudi Canavan thinks like, “it’s only the first book of the trilogy, let’s not rush into things”, which is maddening. I also notice that Trudi Canavan tend to repeat the information/history already mentioned in Black agician trilogy and its prequel. To those who haven’t read them or have but forgot the detail, the repetition might help refreshing your memory, but alas, for those who remember it clearly, the repetition will make you bored.<br /><br />Again, <b>it lacks of action and magic</b> despite a killer/rogue is on the loose and a drug addiction is about to take over the city. <b>It lacks the sense of imminent danger and threat.</b> In fact, some events, like Cery being targeted by the Thief Hunter, Cery’s family being murdered, and Lorkin being almost assassinated and missing, turn out to be not as horrifying as they first suggest, trivial even. Another fatal same mistake: <b>it lacks of real villain.</b> Forget about those attempting to assassinate Lorkin. They are nothing compared to the Ichani pursuing Sonea and Akkarin. One fail assassination, and Lorkin manages to keep going throughout the book safely without any further danger, even though his life is deemed at stake for what his parents did and did not do. They have no backbone at all, the assassins I mean. The Thief Hunter, at first, gave an impression of a frightening figure but as the story progresses and we are getting closer to the truth, it’s just gone with a puff. Like in The Magicians’ Guild, what we think the villain at first turns out to be not the villain, and suddenly a character that is unlikely to be a villain has the potential to be the true villain of the whole trilogy. The difference is, Trudi Canavan only presents Akkarin as the potential villain in The Magicians’ Guild, while this book offers us two (and I don’t know if it is just me but Skellin is so obviously suspicious even from the first meeting).<br /><br />In addition to the usual POVs (Sonea, Rothen, Dannyl, and Cery), the storyline is narrated through Lorkin’s POV as well. I know it is just the first book and a room for character development is still widely open ahead, but in my opinion, Sonea, even Akkarin, gives a stronger impression of character in The Magicians’ Guild than Lorkin does in this book. He is their son, for goodness sake! I think it is fair for the fans to expect him to be… special, and yet he is so normal here. I hope we don’t need to wait for the third book to discover him living up to his parentage, or more, and for the story to be more engaging.<br /><br />What makes this book appealing for the fans of High Lord trilogy is the fact that <b>we are reunited with the characters of the trilogy.</b> It is fun to see how much they change or do not change in that span of twenty years. How things are different now compared to the past. How a rival becomes an ally. How a character shrouded in mystery back then now reveals her true identity. And more importantly, how Akkarin still plays a part in the whole story! <br /><br />I can only give this book three stars but it doesn’t mean I will not read the next book. Trudi Canavan, as far as I can conclude after reading the Black Magician trilogy, tend to write better in the second book and best in the third book of a trilogy. I just hope that I’m not wrong about this trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9589222001397248316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3516725191" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3516725191" />
    <a title="Molly Mortensen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20862217-molly-mortensen"><img alt="Molly Mortensen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380040424p2/20862217.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3516725191?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Molly Mortensen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Molly Mortensen" href="/user/show/20862217-molly-mortensen">Molly Mortensen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20862217-molly-mortensen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20862217-molly-mortensen?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20862217-molly-mortensen?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20862217-molly-mortensen?shelf=2020">2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3516725191&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3516725191" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10684414121296339137">The second series feels more epic fantasy. Not more exciting, but more drawn out and slow. <br/><br/>At the beginning, Lorkin was my favorite, because he was new and wasn't constantly reminiscing like the others. I hoped he'd be somewhat like his father. Nope. He's nice but not real bright. He goes on this whole adventure to do his own thing and not what his mother always tells him. So what does he do then? Falls for the first girl he sees and spends the rest of the book doing what she says. (facepalm) <br/><br/>At</span>
  <span id="freeText10684414121296339137" style="display:none">The second series feels more epic fantasy. Not more exciting, but more drawn out and slow. <br /><br />At the beginning, Lorkin was my favorite, because he was new and wasn't constantly reminiscing like the others. I hoped he'd be somewhat like his father. Nope. He's nice but not real bright. He goes on this whole adventure to do his own thing and not what his mother always tells him. So what does he do then? Falls for the first girl he sees and spends the rest of the book doing what she says. (facepalm) <br /><br />At the beginning, Cery's family was brutally murdered. However from the way he's acting you'd think someone killed his hamster, not his children. He has to be Mr. tough guy and not think about it or grieve. (Sighs) Cery's part is still my favorite, with his investigation into who killed his family. Though I'd expect an underworld Thief to want revenge not justice. <br /><br />Sonea is the most powerful Magician in the guild. So naturally, she's spent the last 20 years doing exactly what they told her, not speaking out, and having zero backbone. What happened to the strong independent young woman from the first books? She's mostly dealing with guild politics in this one and I won't bore you describing that. But by the end, she joins Cery's investigation, which was a welcome change. I don't know why she'd trust Regin though. (You know, the boy who tormented her for years?) It also made no sense how she spent the entire book worrying about her son, only to not seem to care when he told her he probably wouldn't coming home for years, or you know ever.<br /><br />We really don't need Dannyl's Point of view. Its boring and redundant. <br /><br />The big reveal was super obvious and I'm disappointed these apparently smart characters didn't see it sooner. At least there was a real villain, unlike the early books from the first series. <br /><br />Will I read the next one? Maybe eventually, for now I'm switching series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10684414121296339137" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3310445839" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3310445839" />
    <a title="David Harvey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/114133066-david-harvey"><img alt="David Harvey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588265924p2/114133066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3310445839?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Harvey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Harvey" href="/user/show/114133066-david-harvey">David Harvey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3310445839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12430830101044478310">Truth be told, the first 75 pages were a bit dull. However, around the 76 page mark i realised that the slow start was absolutely necessary for someone like me. It helped me to reacquant myself with characters' from the Black Magician trilogy whose details were slightly hazy for me having read the trilogy over 10 years ago. <br/><br/>i enjoy Canavan's ability to speed the story along whilst not missing out on crucial character development. Everything she writes paints a vivid picture of the characters and</span>
  <span id="freeText12430830101044478310" style="display:none">Truth be told, the first 75 pages were a bit dull. However, around the 76 page mark i realised that the slow start was absolutely necessary for someone like me. It helped me to reacquant myself with characters' from the Black Magician trilogy whose details were slightly hazy for me having read the trilogy over 10 years ago. <br /><br />i enjoy Canavan's ability to speed the story along whilst not missing out on crucial character development. Everything she writes paints a vivid picture of the characters and the scenery without getting overly bogged down in the minute details - letting the reader fill in the rest with their imagination. She keeps multiple story lines distinctly separate from each other whilst with a thread of interconnectivity throughout - which was a joy to follow.<br /><br />Lorkin is a fantastic addition to the cast and i'm looking forward to watching his character grow throughout the trilogy.<br /><br />You know the traits of a good book when you can't put it down - and that's exactly what this was for me. Bring on "The Rogue".</span>
