<div id="review_307259030" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/307259030" />
    <a title="Becky (Blogs of a Bookaholic)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8613391-becky-blogs-of-a-bookaholic"><img alt="Becky (Blogs of a Bookaholic)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529956761p2/8613391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/307259030?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky (Blogs of a Bookaholic)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky (Blogs of a Bookaholic)" href="/user/show/8613391-becky-blogs-of-a-bookaholic">Becky (Blogs of a Bookaholic)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Existing fans of The Black Magician Trilogy </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8613391-becky-blogs-of-a-bookaholic?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer307259030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17497719325353501403"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404251280i/10214586.png' width='400' height='171' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This review was originally published on <a href='http://beckysblogs.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blogs of a Bookaholic</a>.<br/><br/><b>Trudi Canavan’s writing still shines among the rubble of some awkward plotting.</b><br/>I am a massive <i>Trudi Canavan</i> fan and have read all of her books since I first discovered the wonderful <i>Black Magician Trilogy</i>. So when I heard that she was releasing a follow up series, I couldn't wait to get started but I have to admit, I was a little bit disappointing by this book. For pure enjoyment it would get 4 stars because I love the author’s style,</span>
  <span id="freeText17497719325353501403" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404251280i/10214586.png" width="400" height="171" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This review was originally published on <a href="http://beckysblogs.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blogs of a Bookaholic</a>.<br><br><b>Trudi Canavan’s writing still shines among the rubble of some awkward plotting.</b><br>I am a massive <i>Trudi Canavan</i> fan and have read all of her books since I first discovered the wonderful <i>Black Magician Trilogy</i>. So when I heard that she was releasing a follow up series, I couldn't wait to get started but I have to admit, I was a little bit disappointing by this book. For pure enjoyment it would get 4 stars because I love the author’s style, however, here in sucky old reality there were a lot of issues holding this book back from being amazing that the reviewer side of my brain couldn't shut off. <br><br>It was so great returning to <i>Canavan’s</i> fantasy world with all of its wonderful elements; the beloved Magician’s Guild, the secret underground network of the Thieves Road and the dangerous foreign lands of Sachaka, and yet…it is all beginning to feel a little…stale. It felt like the same fantasy tropes had been used again that were in her previous books. <br>All the storylines were interesting, but there was no ‘umph’ to them. Each one contains a lot of waiting; waiting for something to happen, waiting to get somewhere or waiting for someone, so that there were few actual events taking place. It seemed as if the author flicking between the four different perspectives was an attempt to disguise that not all that much happened in the book. The pace is consistent, not too slow but not full of action either and I must admit I was hoping for a more definitive ending but instead the story just seemed to stop. The book also retraces a lot of old ground so you don’t feel as if you are gaining that much information. My main problem though, is that it’s not a story in it’s own right – what I mean by that is this book is not a complete story on its own, it needs to be seen as a whole in conjunction with the other two books. <i>The Ambassador’s Mission</i> feels like the stage setup before the concert, and hopefully all that careful planning and considered time will pay off when readers finish the trilogy. Of course, it's still <i>Canavan's</i> work so I still enjoyed it to the point where I struggled to put the book down and found myself reaching for it whenever I had a spare moment.<br><br><i>Trudi Canavan’s</i> writing is awesome as always, I’m pretty sure she could write a book about spreadsheets and I would still be fascinated and glued to the pages. I don’t know what she does or how she does it but I get hooked every time! Her descriptions make me sigh with envy,it’s one of those rare cases where I just revel in the author’s every choice of word and turn of phrase.<br><br>In <i>The Ambassador's Mission</i> We get to reacquaint ourselves with many old characters that we know and love from the original series; Sonea, Dannyl, Cery and Lord Rothen. I was especially surprised that Sonea’s childhood bully Regin played a large role in this book, something I was not expecting at all!<br>Along with these are an interesting cast of new characters, but I don't think they have been developed as well. Unfortunately, this may be a result of including so many of the old characters leaving less room for development of new ones, a bit of a double edged sword. Lorkin, Sonea’s son is the most prominent new character but I failed to connect with him. The only traits he seemed to have were a weakness for the opposite sex and the need to prove himself. He made strange decisions and I wasn't sure if the thought processes were believable. I didn't dislike him, but didn't warm to him either. Tyvara the mysterious woman who abducts Lorkin was a pretty interesting, I loved how unassuming and meek the author presented her and then flipped the character completely and I am looking forward to seeing what’s in store for her, but I didn't warm to her that much either. Cery’s daughter also makes a fun comedic addition with her determination. One thing <i>Canavan</i> does well is her strong female characters. Finally Ashaki Achati the Sachakan was an interesting contrast and gives a great insight into the two different cultures.<br><br>Overall, I'm a bit disappointed but I still love <i>Trudi Cananvan</i>!<br><br><b>You can check out my full, unabridged review and others like it <a href="http://beckysblogs.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blogs of a Bookaholic</a>. :)</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="17497719325353501403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1505726280" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1505726280" />
    <a title="Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38416966-lee"><img alt="Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419697757p2/38416966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1505726280?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/38416966-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1505726280&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1505726280" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10610005902986797850">**spoilers for the whole trilogy**<br/><br/>I've been excited to read this series for ages and couldn't because no libraries near me had the whole set. But fortunately a friend lent me the whole lot and I steamed through them in less than a week. I remember loving Dannyl in the Magicians' Guild trilogy (although I now suspect that was largely teen!me latching onto whatever scraps of queer representation I could find at the time), so I was really looking forward to a series where he's one of the main prota</span>
  <span id="freeText10610005902986797850" style="display:none">**spoilers for the whole trilogy**<br /><br />I've been excited to read this series for ages and couldn't because no libraries near me had the whole set. But fortunately a friend lent me the whole lot and I steamed through them in less than a week. I remember loving Dannyl in the Magicians' Guild trilogy (although I now suspect that was largely teen!me latching onto whatever scraps of queer representation I could find at the time), so I was really looking forward to a series where he's one of the main protagonists. Unfortunately, these days I'm no longer starved for queer protagonists, and it turns out that Dannyl is...kind of boring? And also a rubbish historian who just passively lets his hot would-be boyfriend direct his research and does absolutely nothing to further it himself except casually mention a few times that he's interested in old records. And Tayend feels like a slightly offensive flamboyant stereotype - Canavan *tries* to give him depth, but it never really takes.<br /><br />I don't know, maybe I was just in a bad mood when I read them, because none of the characters really felt alive to me in the way that Sonea did in the first trilogy, not even Sonea (and ugh, god, I needed more build-up than 'Oh he's kind of attractive and no longer an actively terrible human being' to buy Sonea and Regin hooking up). The twenty-year time skip just didn't work for me - it felt like the characters had remained in stasis since the end of the first trilogy, even though Canavan kept trying to make out things had changed so! much!<br /><br />Also, there were at least three points where the copy editor fell asleep on the job - and if I can catch that when I'm meant to be caught up in the story, someone along the line should have corrected that.<br /><br />And despite all that, I kept being eager to come back to them. Despite not really giving a damn about any of the characters (except maybe Anyi), the plot was compelling enough to make me read on. I don't even know why! There were no major plot twists that I didn't predict, and yet I kept wanting to read on. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10610005902986797850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_939404421" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/939404421" />
    <a title="Andrew Riley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19628311-andrew-riley"><img alt="Andrew Riley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366529487p2/19628311.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/939404421?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew Riley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew Riley" href="/user/show/19628311-andrew-riley">Andrew Riley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer939404421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10143439967702483005">I really enjoyed The Ambassador's Mission, in a large part because of what it was not. It wasn't a retread over the same ground that was the major flaw of The Magician's Apprentice prequal. And it doesn't focus exclusively on another young girl coming unexpectedly into magical powers (common to both Apprentice and The Age of Five series). It's well written as is to be expected and has a nice variety of characters with varying personalities and motivations. There's also more world building here, </span>
  <span id="freeText10143439967702483005" style="display:none">I really enjoyed The Ambassador's Mission, in a large part because of what it was not. It wasn't a retread over the same ground that was the major flaw of The Magician's Apprentice prequal. And it doesn't focus exclusively on another young girl coming unexpectedly into magical powers (common to both Apprentice and The Age of Five series). It's well written as is to be expected and has a nice variety of characters with varying personalities and motivations. There's also more world building here, expanding upon what we know and hinting of future revelations in a way that The Magician's Apprentice didn't quite succeed at.<br /><br />The Ambassador's Mission begins 20 years after the events of The High Lord and follows several view points, Sonea, Ceryn and Dannyl make returns and each hold a branch of the story, Sonea's son Lorkin being the final view point character. Sonea and Ceryn are the focus for the part of the story set in the familiar city of Immaridan, location of the majority of The Black Magician trilogy, while Dannyl and Lorkin take us off to Sachaka. The book starts pulling together the threads left laying around by the other four books set in this world, but it does not require you to remember everything that has come before and would be prefectly readable (if not recommended) on it's own.<br /><br />For those hoping for familiar faces, both Rothen and Regin from The Black Magician get a look in, while the Traitors, a group hinted at in The High Lord and introduced more fully in The Magician's Apprentice are set to be a major focus of the new collection.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10143439967702483005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer13876436428782139237">I would've rated this 3.5 if I could. While I did enjoy reading this book I was a little disappointed because it wasn't as good as I'd hoped, and it definitely didn't compare to the Black Magician Trilogy. <br/><br/>Whilst Lorkin was a interesting new addition to the book, I missed Sonea and thought the small part she had in this story was a waste for a character like her. She's supposedly one of the most powerful magicians in Kyralia and yet she spent the majority of this book doing trivial tasks and wor</span>
  <span id="freeText13876436428782139237" style="display:none">I would've rated this 3.5 if I could. While I did enjoy reading this book I was a little disappointed because it wasn't as good as I'd hoped, and it definitely didn't compare to the Black Magician Trilogy. <br /><br />Whilst Lorkin was a interesting new addition to the book, I missed Sonea and thought the small part she had in this story was a waste for a character like her. She's supposedly one of the most powerful magicians in Kyralia and yet she spent the majority of this book doing trivial tasks and worrying about Lorkin.<br /><br />I didn't find Lorkin's plot as captivating as I did the previous books and it definitely took me a while to get into the story, but I'm hoping this is only because it's the first book and acts as an introduction to the trilogy. I am happy that we get to find out a more about Savara and her origins as that was never revealed in The High Lord, but I can't say I like her people as I find them to be a hypocritcal lot. I suppose this doesn't really bode well for the rest of the trilogy as the plot revolves mainly around them, but I am planning to read them nevertheless.<br /><br />I actually found myself enjoying Cery's plot more than Lorkin's even though it was quite predictable, but then again I had liked his character from The Black Magician's Trilogy and most likely I just found it easier to get into a plot concerning characters I'm already familiar with. But as his plot also continues on into the next book, I'm looking forward to reading it.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7162311027116363335">The Ambassador's Mission is set 20 years after the events in The High Lord, the third book in the Black Magicians trilogy. Sonea now a powerful black magician cannot leave the city of Imardin but instead spends her time working in the hospice treating the sick and injured with her healing powers. Lorkin is the son of Sonea and High Lord Akkarin and now an adult he has completed his training in the guild and is looking for something useful to do and follow in the awkward footsteps of his famous, </span>
  <span id="freeText7162311027116363335" style="display:none">The Ambassador's Mission is set 20 years after the events in The High Lord, the third book in the Black Magicians trilogy. Sonea now a powerful black magician cannot leave the city of Imardin but instead spends her time working in the hospice treating the sick and injured with her healing powers. Lorkin is the son of Sonea and High Lord Akkarin and now an adult he has completed his training in the guild and is looking for something useful to do and follow in the awkward footsteps of his famous, late father. <br /><br />Lord Dannyl accepts the vacant post of Guild Ambassador to the country of Sachaka, traditionally the arch enemies of Kyralia but who have settled on a precarious truce and peace which could be broken at any time. Despite his Mother Sonea's appeals not to, Lorkin volunteers to go to Sachaka with Lord Dannyl as his assistant knowing full well that he must keep his parentage a secret as it could put his life in danger...<br /><br />Meanwhile in Imardin, Cery suffers a family tragedy and discovers there is a rogue magician on the loose murdering thieves in the city and he enlists the help of Sonea and Lord Regin to search.<br /><br />I loved this book, we get reunited with a cast of characters from the first trilogy and some new interesting ones. The first half of the book builds the story and then It becomes very interesting with a great climax and conclusion which leads on into the next book The Rogue.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14046557688313625863">I might be a little to harsh on this book, which is sad for me because I loved The Magician's Apprentice when I read it years ago and I've met Trudi Canavan and she's lovely, but I just felt like nothing interesting happened. At all.<br/><br/>I mean, obviously some things happened to the characters but it felt flat with nothing at stake or really exciting.   <span id="freeText14046557688313625863" style="display:none">I might be a little to harsh on this book, which is sad for me because I loved The Magician's Apprentice when I read it years ago and I've met Trudi Canavan and she's lovely, but I just felt like nothing interesting happened. At all.<br /><br />I mean, obviously some things happened to the characters but it felt flat with nothing at stake or really exciting. I'm sorry if I'm supposed to like Lorkin but his character felt so flat and his storyline a forced emancipation from his mother and the Guild. And he obviously fell into a sort of trap (predicted) but from the look of it he's going to learn some mysterious magic and fall in love with the rebel that saved his life (almost there already). <br /><br />The concept of an almost all-women society should be appealing but I'm not sure yet. Calling them "Traitors" is a little bit weird, even if explained.<br /><br />Maybe I'm wrong and it's going to be totally different but I have small hopes that it's going to get better. <br /><br />Even Sonea's parts, which I enjoyed a little more, felt lifeless. She seemed pretty much emprisoned by the Guild. It looks like she can do whatever she wants but yet not? I don't know how to explain it.<br /><br />Just that her life doesn't seem that good to me and it's a little bit of a let down from what her arrival into the guild showed us in the previous trilogy. She just got sucked by a self-righteous system and that's disappointing.<br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132843654" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1012399297380124542">I have been a fan of Trudi Canaven since the black magician triology while The Ambassador's Mission was a fairly enjoyable read it lacked the substance from her previous books. I enjoyed the different storylines but the plot was slow and choppy. The new characters are dull and one dimensional particularly Lorkin and Tyvara. Sonea, Ceri and Dannyl were just as likeable as they were in the black magician trilogy, Trudi stayed true to their charcters. My main issue was defintely Lorkin who turned o</span>
  <span id="freeText1012399297380124542" style="display:none">I have been a fan of Trudi Canaven since the black magician triology while The Ambassador's Mission was a fairly enjoyable read it lacked the substance from her previous books. I enjoyed the different storylines but the plot was slow and choppy. The new characters are dull and one dimensional particularly Lorkin and Tyvara. Sonea, Ceri and Dannyl were just as likeable as they were in the black magician trilogy, Trudi stayed true to their charcters. My main issue was defintely Lorkin who turned out to be so exceptionly ordinary. His parents Sonea and Akkarin - both amazing for their own reasons, Sonea a girl from the slums who is talented, smart and who has never forgotten her roots. Akkarin a slave for years who managed to escape Sachaka, become high lord and defend his city and people single handedly for years even after he was exiled he gave his life for his city. Then we have their son Lorkin who is average in every possible way and has never had to fight for anything. I still have hope for the next two books now we've been introduced to the new generation of characters- hopefully they will develop further by going through various hardships and trials.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1012399297380124542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7351510-nadya?shelf=2012">2012</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer475063612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10807036822693470186">Trudi Canavan is one of those writers that really grows as she writes. I thoroughly enjoyed the first of her newest trilogy, which starts a couple of years after the 1st trilogy ends. Black Magician Sonea's son is grown, and the city has a rogue. Or possible, a couple of rogues. It also has a deadly addiction threatening to take over the city and/or the Guild. <br/><br/>And a lot of other interesting things happen as well. ;)<br/><br/>It has been a long time since a book kept me so bound that I read it within a few</span>
  <span id="freeText10807036822693470186" style="display:none">Trudi Canavan is one of those writers that really grows as she writes. I thoroughly enjoyed the first of her newest trilogy, which starts a couple of years after the 1st trilogy ends. Black Magician Sonea's son is grown, and the city has a rogue. Or possible, a couple of rogues. It also has a deadly addiction threatening to take over the city and/or the Guild. <br /><br />And a lot of other interesting things happen as well. ;)<br /><br />It has been a long time since a book kept me so bound that I read it within a few days. If you're looking for new fantasy to try out, Trudi Canavan might be the one you should try out. Her writing definitely improves with each book, and although this trilogy (the 3rd one she has written) does not require knowledge of the first trilogy she wrote, it is always good to know the characters that you are dealing with so well. The 2nd trilogy she wrote was The Age of Five, and they were all highly enjoyable reads, keeping the reader spellbound and captivated by the world created. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10807036822693470186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/717475610?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316037815" href="/book/show/9459429-the-ambassador-s-mission">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7359792-kathrin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7359792-kathrin?shelf=series-to-finish">series-to-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7359792-kathrin?shelf=female-author">female-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7359792-kathrin?shelf=21th-century">21th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7359792-kathrin?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer717475610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11198862914036305885">After finishing "The Black Magician Trilogy" I was surprised to learn that there is a sequel series. I liked the characters of the first trilogy a lot and I've got a thing for learning how a society evolves after a few decades. I love the fact that the book spends a lot of time dshowing these changes. <br/><br/>The book follows basically two main plots - Lorkin's mission in Sachaka and Sonea's story back in Imardin. For quite a while I cared way more about the storyline with Sonea and Cery because I could</span>
  <span id="freeText11198862914036305885" style="display:none">After finishing "The Black Magician Trilogy" I was surprised to learn that there is a sequel series. I liked the characters of the first trilogy a lot and I've got a thing for learning how a society evolves after a few decades. I love the fact that the book spends a lot of time dshowing these changes. <br /><br />The book follows basically two main plots - Lorkin's mission in Sachaka and Sonea's story back in Imardin. For quite a while I cared way more about the storyline with Sonea and Cery because I couldn't really say what Lorkin's mission was about. I felt like there were some major information missing on his character. I hope that this will change as the series progresses because I came to like the way his mission developed. <br /><br />I think it's important to have read the first trilogy as well as the books that are connected with it. They offer quite a lot information that is needed to get easier into the story. <br /><br />I hope there'll be a lot more character development in the series but I really liked this book and look forward to read the other books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11198862914036305885" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('t+8JbUhbBt2MYYAtun3ATIrND4qXKCX3VmneqMq6eGuGTZXJLKW35+hxK2E4TxIzzBicvRNWizOSoPNtzGlxrw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qKnHoS/d3Jj7MTT4BeMN/4vRFgp7eYxgIqY7dIF7XJuZC1sFSyNtop8hn7SH0d+AzQSFPf8HIqTmbxaxh6hVXw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/15890.Trudi_Canavan">About Trudi Canavan</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/15890.Trudi_Canavan"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1194378660p3/15890.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/15890.Trudi_Canavan">Trudi Canavan
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2885243328290636396">Trudi Canavan was born in Kew, Melbourne and grew up in Ferntree Gully, a suburb at the foothills of the Dandenongs.<br/><br/>In 1999 she won the Aurealis Award for Best Fantasy Short Story with “Whispers of the Mist Children”. In the same year she was granted a writers residency at Varuna Writers’ Centre in Katoomba, New South Wales.<br/><br/>In November 2001, The Magicians’ Guild was first published in Australia. T</span>
  <span id="freeText2885243328290636396" style="display:none">Trudi Canavan was born in Kew, Melbourne and grew up in Ferntree Gully, a suburb at the foothills of the Dandenongs.<br /><br />In 1999 she won the Aurealis Award for Best Fantasy Short Story with “Whispers of the Mist Children”. In the same year she was granted a writers residency at Varuna Writers’ Centre in Katoomba, New South Wales.<br /><br />In November 2001, The Magicians’ Guild was first published in Australia. The second book of the trilogy, The Novice, was published in June 2002 and was nominated for the Aurealis Award for Best Fantasy Novel. The third book The High Lord was released in January 2003 and was nominated for the Best Novel Ditmar category. All three books entered Australian top ten SF bestseller lists.<br /><br />The Black Magician Trilogy reached the international market in 2004, published by HarperCollins’ EOS imprint in North America and Orbit Books in the UK. The trilogy is now rated by Nielsen BookScan as the most successful debut fantasy series of the last 10 years.<br /><br />Trudi’s second trilogy, Age of the Five, has also enjoyed bestselling success. Priestess of the White reached No.3 in the Sunday Times hardback fiction bestseller list, staying in the top ten for six weeks.<br /><br />In early 2006 Trudi signed a seven-figure contract with Orbit to write the prequel and sequel to the Black Magician Trilogy. The prequel, The Magician’s Apprentice was released in 2009 and won the Best Fantasy Novel category of the Aurealis Awards. She is now working on the sequel trilogy, and planning her next fantasy series, which will be set in an entirely new world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2885243328290636396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
